Step into warm shower and wash with [[ASIN:B00EV1D79A Hibiclens Antimicrobial Skin Liquid Soap, 32 Fluid Ounce]], then rinse completely to ensure a clean and oil free surface to work with.<br /><br />2.) Either shower or bathe in hot water allowing the bathroom or shower stall to fill up with unventilated steam for about 15 minutes, usually while taking the time to relax, terrify others in the house with my singing, or pretending to drown my floating plastic bath duck.<br /><br />3.)   118. I originally bought my Baiden mitten after reading an excellent and popular review for a self-tanning product, in which the author said she used the Baiden to slough before doing her tanning. Although I had apprehensions about buying such an expensive mitt, I did want to try it and do everything she had done to get that great tan. I don't know why I didn't think of it before I ordered the mitten, but once I received it, I immediately remembered the Korean cloths for sloughing that we had used when I grew up (I'm half Korean). They're called Korean Italy cloths, for some strange reason, and as I read on further about how the Baiden would roll off strings of dead skin after a soak in a hot tub, I already knew that the Korean cloths did that as well--very effectively, in fact, and for a helluva lot less money--so, I sent my Baiden back without even trying it.<br /><br />I think it's important to point out that I don't at all dispute the excellent exfoliating abilities of the Baiden mitten. From what I've seen and felt, I really have no doubt whatsoever that the Baiden is a high quality product that does what it says, beautifully. Having said that, though, here's why you might want to consider trying one of these Korean cloths yourself before (or in lieu of) trying the Baiden mitt:<br /><br />Firstly, Korean Italy cloths are fairly easy to find, and are monumentally cheaper than the Baiden--you can buy them in any Korean market, on eBay, or even here on Amazon. I bought mine on eBay for $1.15 ea. + free shipping, but I've seen some that are sold here on Amazon for $8 or $9 and as high as $20, depending on the configuration and quantity...but none nearly so expensive as the $50 Baiden. If you try the KI cloth and don't like it, you're only out a few bucks, and can still move on to the Baiden without feeling you've been ripped off.<br /><br />The cheapest Korean Italy cloths I've found were the ones I bought from eBay; however, it should be noted that every one of my shipments from eBay (I ordered several different variations, from several different vendors) took a couple of weeks to receive. As it turns out, they all came straight from Korea. If you are impatient to get them for the sake of getting started asap with your tan, consider ordering here on Amazon, where you can find quicker shipping times, including a few that qualify for Amazon Prime shipping.<br /><br />A second reason to consider the Korean Italy cloth is that it is completely machine washable, and lasts for YEARS. Speaking personally, this is an important feature, as both the cloth and the mitt MUST capture lots of DNA (aka, dead skin) in its crevices, so I would most definitely want to be able to wash it. Alas, the Baiden has conflicting reviews as to whether it's machine washable (although I did read one review from a person who said that they used a touch of laundry soap on it from time to time). I've even read negative reviews on the Baiden by some that said it became moldy. I'll presume that those were simply due to poor care, but regardless, lack of washability would be a deal-breaker for me, personally.<br /><br />In my original post, a few people commented that they'd tried the Korean Italy cloth and found it far too harsh for their skin, and several did not feel the KI cloths were suitable for exfoliating the face. It's important to know that the Korean Italy cloths are available in varying levels of coarseness, and the color of the cloth typically denotes the level of coarseness:<br />a) Blue is the most coarse, for heavy-duty sloughing on the tougher parts of your body, like arms and legs. Many will find this level unsuitable for any part of their body.<br />b) Green is medium, and what I most commonly use.<br />c) Pink is mild coarseness, and what I've used on my face personally to exfoliate.<br />d) Occasionally you'll find a red one, which is medium coarseness.<br />e) There are a few two-sided colors as well:<br />i) Yellow comes with one side in mild coarseness, the other is medium.<br />ii) If you can find a plaid one, that comes with heavy coarseness on one side, and medium on the other. So if you buy a yellow and a plaid, you've got every grade of coarseness in two cloths, for about $2.30.<br />f) If you find any other colors, the packaging should indicate how course it is.<br /><br />I wanted to close my review with some exfoliating tips, but before I did that I wanted to add that I am not affiliated with any Korean Italy cloth company whatsoever. I would imagine that just about any Korean who might stumble upon this product might have the exact same thought process as I did. I will say, though, that I had put up a review a year or two ago about the Baiden mitten that received a lot of likes and comments, but I discovered today (3/24/15) that it's not up anymore. Not sure how or when that happened. I supposed it's possible I might've accidentally deleted it myself, as I do check my reviews from time to time and even edit or update...but I'd be lying if I said it didn't--at least for a moment--make me go, &#34;Hmmmm....&#34;<br /><br />**********<br />Tips For Using The Cloth:<br /><br />Koreans have been using these cloths for years to exfoliate. My Korean mom used to call it &#34;shining&#34; her skin, and she swore it was the reason her skin was so soft. Some exfoliating tips, and tips for using the cloth:<br /><br />- When exfoliating, be sure to soak in a tub of hot water for at least 1/2 hr (until your fingers and toes are pruned) before exfoliating, or your skin might not slough off as much as you'd like. This is true whether you are using a Baiden mitt or a Korean Italy cloth.<br /><br />- Make sure that there are no bath salts, lotions, creams, or anything else but plain water that you soak in, or the dead skin will not peel off properly. Make the water as hot as you can tolerate comfortably. Additionally, if you wear lotions or creams, you might actually want to take a quick shower with soap BEFORE SOAKING IN THE TUB, to wash the lotion off. Lotion makes the skin too slick to slough off, so you need to eliminate it before attempting to exfoliate.<br /><br />- The Korean Italy cloths can be found in a variety of different configurations, including a mitt, but the one I recommend also happens to be the cheapest and most ubiquitous: that is, a pocket, into which you insert a folded, wet but wrung-out wash cloth, to give it some substance to hold onto. Dragging the rolled cloth across your skin, scrub your skin in long strokes. Just like with the Baiden mitten, you should be able to roll strings of dead skin off of your skin surface as you do this. This is what the KI pocket looks like: [[ASIN:B00LGLOKLM Korean Exfoliating Bath Washcloth [4 pcs] (Green) by TeChef Home]] Since there are so many different configurations of the KI cloth, I've also spotted KI pockets that are larger in size, for you to insert your hand into, like the Baiden. This configuration is not as cheap as the smaller pocket that accepts the wash cloth.<br /><br />- When laundering the cloth, although it's okay to throw it into any load, keep in mind that fabric softener might neutralize a little bit of its coarseness. I recommend washing without the use of any softener. Conversely, though, if you are looking to make your cloth just a tad less rough and scratchy (say, for facial exfoliating), then go ahead and try the softener.e in mild coarseness, the other is medium.<br />ii) If you can find a plaid one, that comes with heavy coarseness on one side, and medium on the other. My Korean mom used to call it &#34;shining&#34; her skin, and she swore it was the reason her skin was so soft. Some exfoliating tips, and tips for using the cloth:<br /><br />- When exfoliating, be sure to soak in a tub of hot water for at least 1/2 hr (until your fingers and toes are pruned) before exfoliating, or your skin might not slough off as much as you'd like. This is true whether you are using a Baiden mitt or a Korean Italy cloth.<br /><br />- Make sure that there are no bath salts, lotions, creams, or anything else but plain water that you soak in, or the dead skin will not peel off properly. Make the water as hot as you can tolerate comfortably. Additionally, if you wear lotions or creams, you might actually want to take a quick shower with soap BEFORE SOAKING IN THE TUB, to wash the lotion off. Lotion makes the skin too slick to slough off, so you need to eliminate it before attempting to exfoliate.<br /><br />- The Korean Italy cloths can be found in a variety of different configurations, including a mitt, but the one I recommend also happens to be the cheapest and most ubiquitous: that is, a pocket, into which you insert a folded, wet but wrung-out wash cloth, to give it some substance to hold onto. Dragging the rolled cloth across your skin, scrub your skin in long strokes. Just like with the Baiden mitten, you should be able to roll strings of dead skin off of your skin surface as you do this. This is what the KI pocket looks like: [[ASIN:B00LGLOKLM Korean Exfoliating Bath Washcloth [4 pcs] (Green) by TeChef Home]] Since there are so many different configurations of the KI cloth, I've also spotted KI pockets that are larger in size, for you to insert your hand into, like the Baiden. This configuration is not as cheap as the smaller pocket that accepts the wash cloth.<br /><br />- When laundering the cloth, although it's okay to throw it into any load, keep in mind that fabric softener might neutralize a little bit of its coarseness. I recommend washing without the use of any softener. Conversely, though, if you are looking to make your cloth just a tad less rough and scratchy (say, for facial exfoliating), then go ahead and try the softener.
